GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*x**c3

## Analysis

The GT expression is:
$$f(x,v) = -0.0459\,v^3 - 1.283\,x^3 - 0.7296\,|v|^{1/3}$$

The key terms are:
1. **x³ term**: straightforward, many candidates have this
2. **v³ term**: a cubic in v (odd function)
3. **|v|^{1/3} term**: a cube root of absolute value

The critical challenge is matching the **|v|^{1/3}** term. Let me examine what functional forms the candidates offer for the v-dependent parts:

Most candidates use combinations of:
- `v` (linear)
- `v³` (cubic)
- `v*Abs(v)` (which is |v|² · sign(v), i.e., v|v|)
- `log(c*v² + 1)` — logarithmic in v²
- `log(c*Abs(v) + 1)` — logarithmic in |v|
- `sin(c*v + c)` — sinusoidal

**None of these can produce |v|^{1/3}.**

Let me verify: Can `log(c*Abs(v) + 1)` approximate |v|^{1/3}? For small |v|, log(c|v|+1) ≈ c|v|, which is linear in |v|, not |v|^{1/3}. These are fundamentally different functions — log is not a power law, and we need **exact** equivalence for all v, not approximation.

Can any combination of `v³`, `v*Abs(v)`, `log(v²+1)`, `log(|v|+1)` sum to give `v³ + |v|^{1/3}`? No. The function |v|^{1/3} has a specific algebraic singularity (infinite derivative) at v=0, while all the candidate building blocks (v, v³, v|v|, log(c|v|+1), log(cv²+1)) have finite or zero derivatives at v=0 (or in the case of log(c|v|+1), a finite one-sided derivative). No finite linear combination of these can reproduce the |v|^{1/3} singularity behavior.

Similarly, `sin(c*v)` is analytic and cannot produce |v|^{1/3}.

Candidates with `v**3` terms (like #1, #2, #8, #10, #11, #20, #42) can match the v³ part but still cannot produce |v|^{1/3}.

**Candidate 42** has `c3*log(c4*v² + 1) + c5*v*Abs(v) + c6*log(c7*v² + 1) + c8*v³`, which combines logs, v|v|, and v³. Even combining two log terms, they remain logarithmic functions and cannot produce |v|^{1/3}.

No candidate contains a term like `Abs(v)**c` with a free exponent parameter that could be set to 1/3, nor any fractional power of |v|.

Therefore, none of the candidates can be made equivalent to the GT.

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO7)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0459*v³ - 1.2831*x³ - 0.7296*|v|^(1/3)`

The GT has three terms: `v³`, `x³`, and `|v|^(1/3)`. No constant offset, no `x`, no `x²`, no `v`, no `t` dependence, etc.

The key challenge is that the GT contains `|v|^(1/3)`, which is a cube root of absolute value. None of the candidates explicitly contain `|v|^(1/3)`. The candidates use combinations of:
- `log(c*v² + 1)`, `log(c*|v| + 1)` — these are logarithmic, not power functions
- `v*|v|` = `v²·sign(v)` — this is an odd power-2 function
- `sin`, `cos`, `tanh`, `exp` — transcendental functions

**Critical question:** Can any combination of `log(c*|v| + 1)`, `log(c*v² + 1)`, `v*|v|`, `v`, `v³`, etc. exactly equal `|v|^(1/3)` for all `v`?

No. `|v|^(1/3)` is a specific algebraic function (a fractional power). Logarithmic functions, polynomial functions, and products like `v*|v|` are all linearly independent from `|v|^(1/3)`. No finite combination of `log`, polynomial, `sin`, `cos`, `exp`, `tanh` functions can exactly reproduce a fractional power function like `|v|^(1/3)` over a continuous domain.

This means **none of the candidates can match the GT**, because none contain the basis function `|v|^(1/3)` (or any equivalent fractional power of `|v|`), and this term cannot be synthesized from the available basis functions.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate systematically:

- **Candidates with `v³` and `log(|v|+1)`** (e.g., 1, 8, 10, 40): `log(c|v|+1)` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)` for any constant.
- **Candidates with `v*|v|` and `log(|v|+1)`** (e.g., 4, 16, 23): `v*|v|` is even-powered (magnitude) with odd sign, not `v³`; and `log` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)`.
- **Candidates with `log(v²+1)` and `log(|v|+1)`** (e.g., 31, 32, 49): combinations of logs cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)` or `v³`.
- **Candidates with `sin` terms** (e.g., 6, 7, 21, 44): `sin` cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)`.
- **Candidates with cross terms** like `v*x`, `v*x²`, `x⁵`, `cos(t)`, etc.: these introduce terms not in GT and cannot be zeroed while maintaining the needed `|v|^(1/3)`.

For every single candidate, the fundamental issue is the same: **`|v|^(1/3)` cannot be expressed as any combination of the basis functions available in any candidate.**
